	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Jehovah's Witnesses</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Christian denomination</div>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em; font-size: 88%; text-align: left;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold">Jehovah's Witnesses</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Jw_headquart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Jw headquart.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Jw_headquart.jpg/220px-Jw_headquart.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8d/Jw_headquart.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="320" data-file-height="240" /></a><div>World headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_New_York" title="Warwick, New York">Warwick</a>, New York</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Classification</th><td><a href="/wiki/Nontrinitarianism" title="Nontrinitarianism">Nontrinitarian</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Orientation</th><td><a href="/wiki/Millenarianism" title="Millenarianism">Millenarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Restorationism" title="Restorationism">Restorationist</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_polity" title="Ecclesiastical polity">Governance</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Governing Body</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Structure</th><td><a href="/wiki/Organizational_structure_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Organizational structure of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Hierarchical</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Region</th><td>Worldwide</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Headquarters</th><td><a href="/wiki/Warwick,_New_York" title="Warwick, New York">Warwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, U.S.</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Founder</th><td><a href="/wiki/Charles_Taze_Russell" title="Charles Taze Russell">Charles Taze Russell</a><sup id="cite_ref-Gale_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gale-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Origin</th><td>1870s <br /><a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania</a>, U.S.</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Branched from</th><td><a href="/wiki/Bible_Student_movement" title="Bible Student movement">Bible Student movement</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Separations</th><td><a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_splinter_groups" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses splinter groups">Jehovah's Witnesses splinter groups</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Congregations</th><td>119,954</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Members</th><td>8,579,909</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space: nowrap;">Official website</th><td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://jw.org/">jw<wbr />.org</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Statistics from <i>2018 Grand Totals</i><sup id="cite_ref-report2018_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Jehovah's Witnesses</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Millenarianism" title="Millenarianism">millenarian</a> <a href="/wiki/Restorationism" title="Restorationism">restorationist</a> <a href="/wiki/Christian_denomination" title="Christian denomination">Christian denomination</a> with <a href="/wiki/Nontrinitarianism" title="Nontrinitarianism">nontrinitarian</a> beliefs distinct from mainstream <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The group reports a worldwide membership of approximately 8.58&#160;million adherents involved in <a href="/wiki/Evangelism" title="Evangelism">evangelism</a> and an annual <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_practices#Memorial_of_Christ&#39;s_death" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses practices">Memorial</a> attendance of over 20&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-report2018_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses are directed by the <a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Governing Body of Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, a group of <a href="/wiki/Elder_(Christianity)#Jehovah&#39;s_Witnesses" title="Elder (Christianity)">elders</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warwick,_New_York" title="Warwick, New York">Warwick</a>, New York, United States, which establishes all doctrines<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> based on its interpretations of the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Penton_1997_61–62_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton_1997_61–62-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> They believe that the destruction of the present world system at <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">Armageddon</a> is imminent, and that the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Kingship_and_kingdom_of_God" title="Kingship and kingdom of God">God's kingdom</a> over the earth is the only solution for all problems faced by humanity.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_Concise_Encyclopedia_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica_Concise_Encyclopedia-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The group emerged from the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Student_movement" title="Bible Student movement">Bible Student movement</a> founded in the late 1870s by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taze_Russell" title="Charles Taze Russell">Charles Taze Russell</a>, who also co-founded <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Bible_and_Tract_Society_of_Pennsylvania" title="Watch Tower Bible and Tract Society of Pennsylvania">Zion's Watch Tower Tract Society</a> in 1881 to organize and print the movement's publications.<sup id="cite_ref-Gale_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gale-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Society_presidency_dispute_(1917)" title="Watch Tower Society presidency dispute (1917)">leadership dispute</a> after Russell's death resulted in several groups breaking away, with <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Franklin_Rutherford" title="Joseph Franklin Rutherford">Joseph Franklin Rutherford</a> retaining control of the Watch Tower Society and its properties.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Rutherford made significant organizational and doctrinal changes, including adoption of the name <i>Jehovah's witnesses</i><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> in 1931 to distinguish them from other Bible Student groups and symbolize a break with the legacy of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taze_Russell#Theology_and_teachings" title="Charles Taze Russell">Russell's traditions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-name1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name1-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-name2_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name2-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-name3_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name3-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jehovah's Witnesses are best known for their door-to-door preaching, distributing literature such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Watchtower" title="The Watchtower">The Watchtower</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Awake!" title="Awake!">Awake!</a></i>, and for refusing <a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">military service</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blood_transfusion" title="Blood transfusion">blood transfusions</a>. They consider the use of <a href="/wiki/Names_of_God_in_Christianity" title="Names of God in Christianity">God's name</a> vital for proper worship. They reject <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinitarianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_conditionalism" title="Christian conditionalism">inherent immortality</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_Hell" title="Christian views on Hell">hellfire</a>, which they consider to be unscriptural doctrines. They do not observe <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Easter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birthday" title="Birthday">birthdays</a> or other holidays and customs they consider to have <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> origins incompatible with Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> They prefer to use their own Bible translation, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_World_Translation_of_the_Holy_Scriptures" title="New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures">New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> although their literature occasionally quotes and cites other Bible translations.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Adherents commonly refer to their body of beliefs as "The Truth" and consider themselves to be "in the Truth".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> They consider secular <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a> to be morally corrupt and under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a>, and most limit their social interaction with non-Witnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Church_discipline" title="Church discipline">Congregational disciplinary actions</a> include <i><a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_congregational_discipline#Disfellowshipping" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and congregational discipline">disfellowshipping</a></i>, their term for formal expulsion and <a href="/wiki/Shunning" title="Shunning">shunning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Baptized individuals who formally leave are considered <i>disassociated</i> and are also shunned. Disfellowshipped and disassociated individuals may eventually be reinstated if deemed repentant.<sup id="cite_ref-shepherd_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shepherd-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The group's position regarding <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objection</a> to military service and refusal to <a href="/wiki/Salute" title="Salute">salute</a> state symbols (like <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flag" title="Flag">flags</a>) has brought it into conflict with some governments.<sup id="cite_ref-aa_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aa-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cit_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cit-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, some Jehovah's Witnesses have been persecuted and their activities are banned or restricted in some countries. Persistent <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_cases_involving_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_by_country" title="Supreme Court cases involving Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses by country">legal challenges by Jehovah's Witnesses</a> have influenced legislation related to <a href="/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights" title="Civil and political rights">civil rights</a> in several countries.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The organization has <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Criticism of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">received criticism</a> regarding biblical translation, doctrines, and alleged coercion of its members. The Watch Tower Society has made various unfulfilled predictions about major biblical events such as Christ's <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">Second Coming</a>, the advent of <a href="/wiki/God%27s_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="God&#39;s Kingdom">God's Kingdom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">Armageddon</a>. Their policies for <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses%27_handling_of_child_sex_abuse" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses&#39; handling of child sex abuse">handling cases of child sexual abuse</a> have been the subject of various formal inquiries.
</p>

<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="History of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">History of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%"><tbody><tr><td style="background:lavender;;padding-top:0.4em;line-height:1.2em">Part of <a href="/wiki/Category:Christianity" title="Category:Christianity">a series</a> on</td></tr><tr><th style="background:lavender;;padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;padding-top:0;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em"><a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a></th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0.2em 0 0.4em"><a href="/wiki/File:Christian_cross.svg" class="image" title="Principal symbol of Christianity"><img alt="Principal symbol of Christianity" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Christian_cross.svg/75px-Christian_cross.svg.png" decoding="async" width="75" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Christian_cross.svg/113px-Christian_cross.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Christian_cross.svg/150px-Christian_cross.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="404" data-file-height="564" /></a></td></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">

<h3><span id="Background_.281870.E2.80.931916.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Background_(1870–1916)">Background (1870–1916)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bible_Student_movement" title="Bible Student movement">Bible Student movement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;"><a href="/wiki/File:C.T._Russell.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/C.T._Russell.gif/182px-C.T._Russell.gif" decoding="async" width="182" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/C.T._Russell.gif/273px-C.T._Russell.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f3/C.T._Russell.gif 2x" data-file-width="319" data-file-height="416" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:C.T._Russell.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_Taze_Russell" title="Charles Taze Russell">Pastor Russell</a>, founder of the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Student_movement" title="Bible Student movement">Watch Tower Society</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1870, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taze_Russell" title="Charles Taze Russell">Charles Taze Russell</a> and others formed a group in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> to study the Bible.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During the course of his ministry, Russell disputed many beliefs of mainstream Christianity including immortality of the soul, hellfire, predestination, the fleshly return of Jesus Christ, the Trinity, and the burning up of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-beckford1874_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beckford1874-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 1876, Russell met <a href="/wiki/Nelson_H._Barbour" title="Nelson H. Barbour">Nelson H. Barbour</a>; later that year they jointly produced the book <i><a href="/wiki/Three_Worlds_(book)" title="Three Worlds (book)">Three Worlds</a>,</i> which combined restitutionist views with <a href="/wiki/End_time" title="End time">end time</a> prophecy. The book taught that God's dealings with humanity were divided <a href="/wiki/Dispensationalism" title="Dispensationalism">dispensationally</a>, each ending with a "harvest," that Christ had returned as an invisible spirit being in 1874<sup id="cite_ref-beckford1874_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beckford1874-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> inaugurating the "harvest of the Gospel age," and that 1914 would mark the end of a 2520-year period called "the Gentile Times,"<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> at which time world society would be replaced by the full establishment of God's kingdom on earth.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in 1878 Russell and Barbour jointly edited a religious journal, <i>Herald of the Morning</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In June 1879 the two split over doctrinal differences, and in July, Russell began publishing the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/The_Watchtower" title="The Watchtower">Zion's Watch Tower and Herald of Christ's Presence</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Holden18_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden18-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> stating that its purpose was to demonstrate that the world was in "the last days," and that a new age of earthly and human restitution under the reign of Christ was imminent.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1879, <i>Watch Tower</i> supporters gathered as autonomous congregations to study the Bible topically. Thirty congregations were founded, and during 1879 and 1880, Russell visited each to provide the format he recommended for conducting meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 1881, <i>Zion's Watch Tower Tract Society</i> was presided over by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Conley" title="William Henry Conley">William Henry Conley</a>, and in 1884, Russell incorporated the society as a non-profit business to distribute tracts and Bibles.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> By about 1900, Russell had organized thousands of part- and full-time <a href="/wiki/Colporteur" class="mw-redirect" title="Colporteur">colporteurs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Holden18_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden18-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and was appointing foreign <a href="/wiki/Missionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Missionaries">missionaries</a> and establishing branch offices. By the 1910s, Russell's organization maintained nearly a hundred "pilgrims," or traveling preachers.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Russell engaged in significant global publishing efforts during his ministry,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and by 1912, he was the most distributed Christian author in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Russell moved the Watch Tower Society's headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York, in 1909, combining printing and corporate offices with a house of worship; volunteers were housed in a nearby residence he named <i>Bethel</i>. He identified the religious movement as "Bible Students," and more formally as the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Student_movement#International_Bible_Students_Association" title="Bible Student movement">International Bible Students Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> By 1910, about 50,000 people worldwide were associated with the movement<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and congregations re-elected him annually as their "pastor."<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Russell died October 31, 1916, at the age of 64 while returning from a ministerial speaking tour.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Reorganization_.281917.E2.80.931942.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Reorganization_(1917–1942)">Reorganization (1917–1942)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;"><a href="/wiki/File:J.F._Rutherford.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/J.F._Rutherford.gif/182px-J.F._Rutherford.gif" decoding="async" width="182" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/J.F._Rutherford.gif/273px-J.F._Rutherford.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/J.F._Rutherford.gif 2x" data-file-width="306" data-file-height="461" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:J.F._Rutherford.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Franklin_Rutherford" title="Joseph Franklin Rutherford">Joseph F. Rutherford</a>, founder of Jehovah's Witnesses</div></div></div>
<p>In January 1917, the Watch Tower Society's legal representative, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Franklin_Rutherford" title="Joseph Franklin Rutherford">Joseph Franklin Rutherford</a>, was elected as its next president. His <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Society_presidency_dispute_(1917)" title="Watch Tower Society presidency dispute (1917)">election was disputed</a>, and members of the Board of Directors accused him of acting in an autocratic and secretive manner.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The divisions between his supporters and opponents triggered a major turnover of members over the next decade.<sup id="cite_ref-crompton101_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crompton101-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Penton_1997_61–62_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton_1997_61–62-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In June 1917, he released <i>The Finished Mystery</i> as a seventh volume of Russell's <i><a href="/wiki/Studies_in_the_Scriptures" title="Studies in the Scriptures">Studies in the Scriptures</a></i> series. The book, published as the posthumous work of Russell, was a compilation of his commentaries on the Bible books of <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Ezekiel" title="Book of Ezekiel">Ezekiel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">Revelation</a>, plus numerous additions by Bible Students Clayton Woodworth and George Fisher.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> It strongly criticized Catholic and Protestant clergy and Christian involvement in the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">Great War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As a result, Watch Tower Society directors were jailed for <a href="/wiki/Sedition" title="Sedition">sedition</a> under the <i><a href="/wiki/Espionage_Act_of_1917" title="Espionage Act of 1917">Espionage Act</a></i> in 1918 and members were subjected to mob violence; the directors were released in March 1919 and charges against them were dropped in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rutherford centralized organizational control of the Watch Tower Society. In 1919, he instituted the appointment of a director in each congregation, and a year later all members were instructed to report their weekly preaching activity to the Brooklyn headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-Franz,_Raymond_2007_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Franz,_Raymond_2007-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> At an international convention held at <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Point" title="Cedar Point">Cedar Point</a>, Ohio, in September 1922, a new emphasis was made on house-to-house preaching.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Significant changes in doctrine and administration were regularly introduced during Rutherford's twenty-five years as president, including the 1920 announcement that the Hebrew patriarchs (such as <a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">Abraham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isaac" title="Isaac">Isaac</a>) would be resurrected in 1925, marking the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ">Christ</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Millennialism" title="Millennialism">thousand-year earthly Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rutherford1920_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rutherford1920-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-christian144_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-christian144-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Because of disappointment over the changes and <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Society_unfulfilled_predictions#1925:_Resurrection_of_the_patriarchs" title="Watch Tower Society unfulfilled predictions">unfulfilled predictions</a>, tens of thousands of defections occurred during the first half of Rutherford's tenure, leading to the formation of several Bible Student organizations independent of the Watch Tower Society,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Penton,_1997,_58_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton,_1997,_58-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gruss2001_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruss2001-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> most of which still exist.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> By mid-1919, as many as one in seven of Russell-era Bible Students had ceased their association with the Society, and as many as three-quarters by the end of the 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Penton,_1997,_58_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton,_1997,_58-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 26, 1931, at a convention in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus</a>, Ohio, Rutherford introduced the new name – <i>Jehovah's witnesses</i> – based on <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">Isaiah</a> 43:10: "'You are my witnesses,' declares Jehovah, 'Yes, my servant whom I have chosen, So that you may know and have faith in me And understand that I am the same One. Before me no God was formed, And after me there has been none.'" (New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures 2013 Edition) —which was adopted by resolution. The name was chosen to distinguish his group of Bible Students from other independent groups that had severed ties with the Society, as well as symbolize the instigation of new outlooks and the promotion of fresh evangelizing methods.<sup id="cite_ref-name1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name1-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-name2_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name2-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-name3_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-name3-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 1932, Rutherford eliminated the system of locally elected elders and in 1938, introduced what he called a "theocratic" (literally, <i>God-ruled</i>) organizational system, under which appointments in congregations worldwide were made from the Brooklyn headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-Franz,_Raymond_2007_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Franz,_Raymond_2007-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1932, it was taught that the "little flock" of 144,000 would not be the only people to survive Armageddon. Rutherford explained that in addition to the 144,000 "anointed" who would be resurrected—or transferred at death—to live in heaven to rule over earth with Christ, a separate class of members, the "great multitude," would live in a paradise restored on earth; from 1935, new converts to the movement were considered part of that class.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> By the mid-1930s, the timing of the beginning of Christ's presence (Greek: <i>parousía</i>), his enthronement as king, and the start of the "<a href="/wiki/End_times" class="mw-redirect" title="End times">last days</a>" were each moved to 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:130px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NathanHomerKnorr-WTPres.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/87/NathanHomerKnorr-WTPres.png" decoding="async" width="128" height="167" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="128" data-file-height="167" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NathanHomerKnorr-WTPres.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nathan_Homer_Knorr" title="Nathan Homer Knorr">Nathan H. Knorr</a>, the third president of the <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Bible_and_Tract_Society_of_Pennsylvania" title="Watch Tower Bible and Tract Society of Pennsylvania">Watch Tower Society</a></div></div></div>
<p>As their interpretations of the Bible evolved, Witness publications decreed that saluting national flags is a form of idolatry, which led to a new outbreak of mob violence and government opposition in the United States, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Worldwide membership of Jehovah's Witnesses reached 113,624 in 5,323 congregations by the time of Rutherford's death in January 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Continued_development_.281942.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_development_(1942–present)">Continued development (1942–present)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Development_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_doctrine" title="Development of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses doctrine">Development of Jehovah's Witnesses doctrine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Governing Body of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nathan_H._Knorr" class="mw-redirect" title="Nathan H. Knorr">Nathan Knorr</a> was appointed as third president of the Watch Tower Bible and Tract Society in 1942. Knorr commissioned a new translation of the Bible, the <i><a href="/wiki/New_World_Translation_of_the_Holy_Scriptures" title="New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures">New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures</a></i>, the full version of which was released in 1961. He organized large international assemblies, instituted new training programs for members, and expanded missionary activity and branch offices throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Knorr's presidency was also marked by an increasing use of explicit instructions guiding Witnesses in their lifestyle and conduct, and a greater use of <a href="/wiki/Church_discipline" title="Church discipline">congregational judicial procedures</a> to enforce a strict moral code.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1966, Witness publications and convention talks built anticipation of the possibility that Christ's thousand-year reign might begin in late 1975<sup id="cite_ref-Georgie_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgie-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> or shortly thereafter.<sup id="cite_ref-Penton,_1997,_95_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton,_1997,_95-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The number of baptisms increased significantly, from about 59,000 in 1966 to more than 297,000 in 1974. By 1975, the number of active members exceeded two million. Membership declined during the late 1970s after expectations for 1975 were proved wrong.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stark_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stark-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Watch Tower Society literature did not state dogmatically that 1975 would definitely mark the end,<sup id="cite_ref-Penton,_1997,_95_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton,_1997,_95-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> but in 1980 the Watch Tower Society admitted its responsibility in building up hope regarding that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Hans_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hans-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The offices of elder and ministerial servant were restored to Witness congregations in 1972, with appointments made from headquarters<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> (and later, also by branch committees). It was announced that, starting in September 2014, appointments would be made by traveling overseers. In a major organizational overhaul in 1976, the power of the Watch Tower Society president was diminished, with authority for doctrinal and organizational decisions passed to the <a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Governing Body</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Since Knorr's death in 1977, the position of president has been occupied by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_Franz" title="Frederick William Franz">Frederick Franz</a> (1977–1992) and <a href="/wiki/Milton_George_Henschel" title="Milton George Henschel">Milton Henschel</a> (1992–2000), both members of the Governing Body, and since 2000 by others who are not Governing Body members. In 1995, Jehovah's Witnesses abandoned the idea that Armageddon must occur during the lives of the generation that was alive in 1914 and in 2010 changed their teaching on the "generation".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span></h2>

Opposition</th></tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em;background:#EDEDED;padding-top:0.1em;padding-bottom:0.5em;">

</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Template:Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Template talk:Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Jehovah%27s_Witnesses&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Organizational_structure_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Organizational structure of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Organizational structure of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses are organized <a href="/wiki/Hierarchy" title="Hierarchy">hierarchically</a>, in what the leadership calls a "theocratic organization", reflecting their belief that it is God's "visible organization" on earth.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pentongov_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentongov-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The organization is led by the <a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Governing Body</a>—an all-male group that varies in size, but since January 2018 has comprised eight members,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> all of whom profess to be of the "anointed" class with a hope of heavenly life—based in the Watch Tower Society's Warwick headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> There is no election for membership; new members are selected by the existing body.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Until late 2012, the Governing Body described itself as the representative<sup id="cite_ref-GB2008_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GB2008-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> and "spokesman" for God's "<a href="/wiki/Faithful_and_discreet_slave" title="Faithful and discreet slave">faithful and discreet slave</a> class" (then approximately 10,000 self-professed <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_salvation#The_&#39;anointed&#39;" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and salvation">"anointed" Jehovah's Witnesses</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> At the 2012 Annual Meeting of the Watch Tower Society, the "faithful and discreet slave" was defined as referring to the Governing Body only.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The Governing Body directs several committees that are responsible for administrative functions, including publishing, assembly programs and evangelizing activities.<sup id="cite_ref-pentongov_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentongov-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> It appoints all branch committee members and traveling overseers, after they have been recommended by local branches, with traveling overseers supervising circuits of congregations within their jurisdictions. Traveling overseers appoint local elders and ministerial servants, and while branch offices may appoint regional committees for matters such as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hall" title="Kingdom Hall">Kingdom Hall</a> construction or disaster relief.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The leadership and supporting staff lives in properties owned by the organization worldwide referred to as "Bethel" where they operate as a religious community and administrative unit.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Their living expenses and those of other full-time volunteers are covered by the organization along with a basic monthly <a href="/wiki/Stipend" title="Stipend">stipend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each congregation has a body of appointed unpaid male elders and ministerial servants. Elders maintain general responsibility for congregational governance, setting meeting times, selecting speakers and conducting meetings, directing the public preaching work, and creating "judicial committees" to investigate and decide disciplinary action for cases involving sexual misconduct or doctrinal breaches.<sup id="cite_ref-alternative_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alternative-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> New elders are appointed by a traveling overseer after recommendation by the existing body of elders. Ministerial servants—appointed in a similar manner to elders—fulfill clerical and attendant duties, but may also teach and conduct meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-pentongov_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentongov-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses do not use <i>elder</i> as a title to signify a formal clergy-laity division,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> though elders may employ <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_privilege" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecclesiastical privilege">ecclesiastical privilege</a> regarding confession of sins.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">Baptism</a> is a requirement for being considered a member of Jehovah's Witnesses. Jehovah's Witnesses do not practice infant baptism,<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> and previous baptisms performed by other denominations are not considered valid.<sup id="cite_ref-RFbaptism_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFbaptism-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Individuals undergoing baptism must affirm publicly that dedication and baptism identify them "as one of Jehovah's Witnesses in association with God's spirit-directed organization,"<sup id="cite_ref-RFbaptism_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFbaptism-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> though Witness publications say baptism symbolizes personal dedication to God and not "to a man, work or organization."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Their literature emphasizes the need for members to be obedient and loyal to Jehovah and to "his organization,"<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup> stating that individuals must remain part of it to receive God's favor and to survive Armageddon.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publishing">Publishing</span></h3>
<p>The organization produces a significant amount of literature as part of its evangelism activities.<sup id="cite_ref-pub_titans_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pub_titans-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The Watch Tower Society has produced over 220 million copies of the <i>New World Translation</i> in whole or in part in over 160 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Watchtower" title="The Watchtower">The Watchtower</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Awake!" title="Awake!">Awake!</a></i> are the most widely distributed magazines in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Translation of Witness publications is done by over 2000 volunteers worldwide, producing literature in several hundred languages.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Publications are also available online at the organization's official website.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span></h3>
<p>Much of their funding is provided by <a href="/wiki/Donation" title="Donation">donations</a>, primarily from members. There is no <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">tithing</a> or collection.<sup id="cite_ref-Hans_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hans-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In 2001 <i><a href="/wiki/Newsday" title="Newsday">Newsday</a></i> listed the Watch Tower Society as one of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>'s forty richest corporations, with revenues exceeding $950 million.<sup id="cite_ref-pub_titans_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pub_titans-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> The organization reported for the same year that it "spent over $70.9 million in caring for special pioneers, missionaries, and traveling overseers in their field service assignments."<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Beliefs">Beliefs</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_beliefs" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses beliefs">Jehovah's Witnesses beliefs</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sources_of_doctrine">Sources of doctrine</span></h3>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe their denomination is a restoration of <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_1st_century" title="Christianity in the 1st century">first-century Christianity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Doctrine" title="Doctrine">Doctrines</a> of Jehovah's Witnesses are established by the <a href="/wiki/Governing_Body_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Governing Body of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Governing Body</a>, which assumes responsibility for <a href="/wiki/Exegesis" title="Exegesis">interpreting</a> and applying scripture.<sup id="cite_ref-Penton_1997_61–62_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Penton_1997_61–62-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The Governing Body does not issue any single, comprehensive "statement of faith", but prefers to express its doctrinal position in a variety of ways through publications published by the Watch Tower Society.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Their publications teach that doctrinal changes and refinements result from a process of progressive <a href="/wiki/Revelation" title="Revelation">revelation</a>, in which God gradually reveals his will and purpose,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> and that such enlightenment or "new light"<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> results from the application of <a href="/wiki/Reason" title="Reason">reason</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biblical_studies" title="Biblical studies">study</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> the guidance of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_spirit" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy spirit">holy spirit</a>, and direction from <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ">Jesus Christ</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angels" class="mw-redirect" title="Angels">angels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The Society also teaches that members of the Governing Body are helped by the holy spirit to discern "deep truths", which are then considered by the entire Governing Body before it makes doctrinal decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The group's leadership, while disclaiming divine inspiration and <a href="/wiki/Infallibility_of_the_Church" title="Infallibility of the Church">infallibility</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> is said to provide "divine guidance"<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> through its teachings described as "based on God's Word thus ... not from men, but from Jehovah."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-voice_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voice-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The entire Protestant <a href="/wiki/Biblical_canon" title="Biblical canon">canon of scripture</a> is considered the <a href="/wiki/Biblical_inspiration" title="Biblical inspiration">inspired</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biblical_inerrancy" title="Biblical inerrancy">inerrant</a> word of God.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses consider the Bible to be <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_Bible#The_Bible_and_science" title="Criticism of the Bible">scientifically</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Bible_and_history" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bible and history">historically</a> accurate and reliable<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> and interpret much of it <a href="/wiki/Biblical_literalism" title="Biblical literalism">literally</a>, but accept parts of it as <a href="/wiki/Allegorical_interpretation_of_the_Bible" title="Allegorical interpretation of the Bible">symbolic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> They consider the Bible to be the final authority for all their beliefs,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> although sociologist Andrew Holden's <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">ethnographic</a> study of the group concluded that pronouncements of the Governing Body, through Watch Tower Society publications, carry almost as much weight as the Bible.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Regular personal Bible reading is frequently recommended; Witnesses are discouraged from formulating doctrines and "private ideas" reached through Bible research independent of Watch Tower Society publications, and are cautioned against reading other religious literature.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevindependent_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevindependent-165">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Adherents are told to have "complete confidence" in the leadership, avoid skepticism about what is taught in the Watch Tower Society's literature, and "not advocate or insist on personal opinions or harbor private ideas when it comes to Bible understanding."<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The organization makes no provision for members to criticize or contribute to official teachings<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> and all Witnesses must abide by its doctrines and organizational requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-w89_0401_1_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-w89_0401_1-173">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jehovah_and_Jesus">Jehovah and Jesus</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:144px;"><a href="/wiki/File:YHWH.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/YHWH.svg/142px-YHWH.svg.png" decoding="async" width="142" height="59" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/YHWH.svg/213px-YHWH.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/YHWH.svg/284px-YHWH.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="612" data-file-height="256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:YHWH.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Tetragrammaton" title="Tetragrammaton">Tetragrammaton</a></div></div></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses emphasize the use of God's name, and they prefer the form <i><a href="/wiki/Jehovah" title="Jehovah">Jehovah</a></i>&#8212;a vocalization of <a href="/wiki/God_in_Christianity" title="God in Christianity">God</a>'s name based on the <a href="/wiki/Tetragrammaton" title="Tetragrammaton">Tetragrammaton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> They believe that Jehovah is the only true God, the creator of all things, and the "Universal Sovereign". They believe that all worship should be directed toward him, and that he is not part of a <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinity</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> consequently, the group places more emphasis on God than on Christ.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> They believe that the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit_in_Christianity" title="Holy Spirit in Christianity">Holy Spirit</a> is God's applied power or "active force", rather than a person.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe that <a href="/wiki/Jesus_in_Christianity" title="Jesus in Christianity">Jesus</a> is God's only direct creation, that everything else was created through Christ by means of God's power, and that the initial unassisted act of creation uniquely identifies Jesus as God's "only-begotten Son".<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Jesus served as a <a href="/wiki/Redeemer_(Christianity)" title="Redeemer (Christianity)">redeemer</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Ransom_theory_of_atonement" title="Ransom theory of atonement">ransom sacrifice</a> to pay for the sins of humanity.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> They believe Jesus died on a <a href="/wiki/Instrument_of_Jesus%27_crucifixion" title="Instrument of Jesus&#39; crucifixion">single upright post</a> rather than the traditional <a href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Jesus" title="Crucifixion of Jesus">cross</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Biblical references to the <a href="/wiki/Michael_(archangel)" title="Michael (archangel)">Archangel Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abaddon" title="Abaddon">Abaddon</a> (Apollyon), and <a href="/wiki/Christ_the_Logos" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ the Logos">the Word</a> are interpreted as names for Jesus in various roles.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Jesus is considered to be the only <a href="/wiki/Intercession" title="Intercession">intercessor</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_priest" title="High priest">high priest</a> between God and humanity, and appointed by God as the king and judge of his kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> His role as a mediator (referred to in 1 Timothy 2:5) is applied to the 'anointed' class, though the 'other sheep' are said to also benefit from the arrangement.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Satan">Satan</span></h3>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe that <a href="/wiki/Devil_in_Christianity" title="Devil in Christianity">Satan</a> was originally a perfect <a href="/wiki/Angel" title="Angel">angel</a> who developed feelings of self-importance and craved worship. Satan influenced <a href="/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" title="Adam and Eve">Adam and Eve</a> to disobey God, and humanity subsequently became participants in a challenge involving the competing claims of Jehovah and Satan to universal sovereignty.<sup id="cite_ref-pentonsatan_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentonsatan-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Other angels who sided with Satan became <a href="/wiki/Demon" title="Demon">demons</a>.
</p><p>Jehovah's Witnesses teach that Satan and his demons were cast down to earth from heaven after October 1, 1914,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> at which point the <a href="/wiki/End_time" title="End time">end times</a> began. They believe that Satan is the ruler of the current world order,<sup id="cite_ref-pentonsatan_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentonsatan-188">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> that human society is influenced and misled by Satan and his demons, and that they are a cause of human suffering. They also believe that human governments are controlled by Satan,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> but that he does not directly control each human ruler.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_after_death">Life after death</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_salvation" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and salvation">Jehovah's Witnesses and salvation</a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe death is a state of non-existence with no <a href="/wiki/Consciousness" title="Consciousness">consciousness</a>. There is no <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_hell" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian views on hell">Hell</a> of fiery torment; <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_Hades" title="Christian views on Hades">Hades</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheol" title="Sheol">Sheol</a> are understood to refer to the condition of death, termed the <i>common grave</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses consider the <a href="/wiki/Soul_(spirit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Soul (spirit)">soul</a> to be a life or a living body that can die.<sup id="cite_ref-hoeksin_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoeksin-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses believe that humanity is in a <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_of_sin#Protestant_views" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian views of sin">sinful</a> state,<sup id="cite_ref-hoeksin_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoeksin-193">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> from which release is only possible by means of Jesus' shed blood as a ransom, or <a href="/wiki/Substitutionary_atonement" title="Substitutionary atonement">atonement</a>, for the sins of humankind.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Witnesses believe that a "little flock" of 144,000 selected humans go to heaven, but that the majority (the "other sheep") are to be resurrected by God to a cleansed earth after Armageddon. They interpret <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">Revelation</a> 14:1–5 to mean that the number of Christians going to heaven is limited to exactly 144,000, who will rule with Jesus as kings and priests over earth.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> They believe that baptism as one of Jehovah's Witnesses is vital for salvation<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> and that only they meet scriptural requirements for surviving Armageddon, but that God is the final judge.<sup id="cite_ref-onlyjw_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onlyjw-197">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> During Christ's <a href="/wiki/Millennialism" title="Millennialism">millennial reign</a>, most people who died prior to Armageddon will be resurrected with the prospect of living forever; they will be taught the proper way to worship God to prepare them for their final test at the end of the millennium.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="God.27s_Kingdom"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="God's_Kingdom">God's Kingdom</span></h3>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe that <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_God" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of God">God's Kingdom</a> is a literal government in heaven, ruled by Jesus Christ and 144,000 "spirit-anointed" Christians drawn from the earth, which they associate with Jesus' reference to a "new covenant".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> The kingdom is viewed as the means by which God will accomplish his original purpose for the earth, transforming it into a paradise without sickness or death.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> It is said to have been the focal point of Jesus' ministry on earth.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> They believe the kingdom was established in heaven in 1914,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> and that Jehovah's Witnesses serve as representatives of the kingdom on earth.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eschatology">Eschatology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eschatology_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Eschatology of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Eschatology of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<p>A central teaching of Jehovah's Witnesses is that the current world era, or "system of things", entered the "<a href="/wiki/End_time" title="End time">last days</a>" in 1914 and faces imminent destruction through intervention by God and Jesus Christ, leading to deliverance for those who worship God acceptably.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> They consider all other present-day religions to be false, identifying them with "<a href="/wiki/Whore_of_Babylon#Jehovah&#39;s_Witnesses" title="Whore of Babylon">Babylon the Great</a>", or the "harlot", of Revelation&#160;17,<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> and believe that they will soon be destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, which they believe is represented in scripture by the <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_the_United_Nations" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and the United Nations">scarlet-colored wild beast</a> of Revelation chapter 17. This development will mark the beginning of the "<a href="/wiki/Great_tribulation" class="mw-redirect" title="Great tribulation">great tribulation</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Satan will subsequently use world governments to attack Jehovah's Witnesses, an action that will prompt God to begin the war of <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">Armageddon</a>, during which all forms of government and all people not counted as Christ's "sheep" will be destroyed. After Armageddon, God will extend his heavenly kingdom to include earth, which will be transformed into a paradise similar to the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Most of those who had died before God's intervention will gradually be resurrected during the <a href="/wiki/Millenarianism" title="Millenarianism">thousand year</a> "judgment day". This judgment will be based on their actions after resurrection rather than past deeds. At the end of the thousand years, Christ will hand all authority back to God. Then a final test will take place when Satan is released to mislead perfect mankind. Those who fail will be destroyed, along with Satan and his demons. The end result will be a fully tested, glorified human race on earth.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe that Jesus Christ began to rule in heaven as king of God's kingdom in October 1914, and that Satan was subsequently ousted from heaven to the earth, resulting in "woe" to humanity. They believe that Jesus rules invisibly, from heaven, perceived only as a series of "signs". They base this belief on a rendering of the Greek word <i><a href="/wiki/Parousia" title="Parousia">parousia</a></i>—usually translated as "coming" when referring to Christ—as "presence". They believe Jesus' presence includes an unknown period beginning with his inauguration as king in heaven in 1914, and ending when he comes to bring a final judgment against humans on earth. They thus depart from the mainstream Christian belief that the "<a href="/wiki/Second_coming" class="mw-redirect" title="Second coming">second coming</a>" of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Matthew</a> 24 refers to a single moment of arrival on earth to judge humans.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Practices">Practices</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_practices" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses practices">Jehovah's Witnesses practices</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Worship">Worship</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg/220px-Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg/330px-Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg/440px-Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reuni%C3%A3o_em_Sal%C3%A3o_do_Reino.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Worship at a <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hall" title="Kingdom Hall">Kingdom Hall</a></div></div></div>
<p>Meetings for worship and study are held at <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hall" title="Kingdom Hall">Kingdom Halls</a>, which are typically functional in character, and do not contain religious symbols.<sup id="cite_ref-holdenhall_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holdenhall-218">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses are assigned to a congregation in whose "territory" they usually reside and attend weekly services they refer to as "meetings" as scheduled by congregation elders. The meetings are largely devoted to study of Watch Tower Society literature and the Bible. The format of the meetings is established by the group's headquarters, and the subject matter for most meetings is the same worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-holdenhall_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holdenhall-218">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Congregations meet for two sessions each week comprising four distinct meetings that total about three-and-a-half hours, typically gathering mid-week (two meetings) and on the weekend (two meetings). Prior to 2009, congregations met three times each week; these meetings were condensed, with the intention that members dedicate an evening for "family worship".<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Gatherings are opened and closed with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom songs">kingdom songs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hymns" class="mw-redirect" title="Hymns">hymns</a>) and brief prayers. Twice each year, Witnesses from a number of congregations that form a "circuit" gather for a one-day assembly. Larger groups of congregations meet once a year for a three-day "regional convention", usually at rented stadiums or auditoriums.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Their most important and solemn event is the commemoration of the "Lord's Evening Meal", or "<a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_practices#Memorial_of_Christ&#39;s_death" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses practices">Memorial of Christ's Death</a>" on the date of the Jewish <a href="/wiki/Passover" title="Passover">Passover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evangelism">Evangelism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_publications" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses publications">Jehovah's Witnesses publications</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg/220px-Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg/330px-Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg/440px-Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_outside_the_British_Museum_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jehovah's Witnesses outside the British Museum, 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses are perhaps best known for their <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">efforts to spread their beliefs</a>, most notably by visiting people from house to house,<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> distributing literature published by the Watch Tower Society in 700 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> The objective is to start a regular "Bible study" with any person who is not already a member,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> with the intention that the student be baptized as a member of the group;<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses are advised to consider discontinuing Bible studies with students who show no interest in becoming members.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses are taught they are under a biblical command to engage in public preaching.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> They are instructed to devote as much time as possible to their ministry and are required to submit an individual monthly "Field Service Report".<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Baptized members who fail to report a month of preaching are termed "irregular" and may be counseled by elders;<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> those who do not submit reports for six consecutive months are termed "inactive".<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethics_and_morality">Ethics and morality</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_congregational_discipline#Discipline_involving_&quot;serious_sin&quot;" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and congregational discipline">Jehovah's Witnesses list of "serious sins"</a></div>
