<p>All sexual relations outside of marriage are grounds for expulsion if the individual is not deemed repentant;<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Watchtower_1998,_page_16_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Watchtower_1998,_page_16-240">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexual</a> activity is considered a serious sin, and <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriages</a> are forbidden. <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">Abortion</a> is considered <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-holdenmorals_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holdenmorals-241">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">Suicide</a> is considered to be "self-murder" and a sin against God.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Modesty in dress and grooming is frequently emphasized. <a href="/wiki/Gambling" title="Gambling">Gambling</a>, drunkenness, illegal drugs, and tobacco use are forbidden.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Drinking of <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic beverages</a> is permitted in moderation.<sup id="cite_ref-holdenmorals_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holdenmorals-241">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The family structure is <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchal</a>. The husband is considered to have authority on family decisions, but is encouraged to solicit his wife's thoughts and feelings, as well as those of his children. Marriages are required to be <a href="/wiki/Monogamy" title="Monogamy">monogamous</a> and legally <a href="/wiki/Civil_registry" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil registry">registered</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Marrying a non-believer, or endorsing such a union, is strongly discouraged and carries religious sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Divorce" title="Divorce">Divorce</a> is discouraged, and remarriage is forbidden unless a divorce is obtained on the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">adultery</a>, which they refer to as "a scriptural divorce".<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> If a divorce is obtained for any other reason, remarriage is considered adulterous unless the prior spouse has died or is since considered to have committed <a href="/wiki/Sexual_ethics" title="Sexual ethics">sexual immorality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Extreme physical abuse, willful non-support of one's family, and what the denomination terms "absolute endangerment of spirituality" are considered grounds for legal separation.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Disciplinary_action">Disciplinary action</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_congregational_discipline" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and congregational discipline">Jehovah's Witnesses and congregational discipline</a></div>
<p>Formal discipline is administered by congregation elders. When a baptized member is accused of committing a <a href="/wiki/Mortal_sin#Jehovah&#39;s_Witnesses" title="Mortal sin">serious sin</a>—usually cases of sexual misconduct<sup id="cite_ref-alternative_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alternative-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> or charges of <a href="/wiki/Apostasy" title="Apostasy">apostasy</a> for disputing Jehovah's Witness doctrines<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Muramoto_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muramoto-254">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>—a judicial committee is formed to determine guilt, provide help and possibly administer discipline. <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_congregational_discipline#Disfellowshipping" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and congregational discipline">Disfellowshipping</a>, a form of <a href="/wiki/Shunning" title="Shunning">shunning</a>, is the strongest form of discipline, administered to an offender deemed unrepentant.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Contact with disfellowshipped individuals is limited to direct family members living in the same home, and with congregation elders who may invite disfellowshipped persons to apply for reinstatement;<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> formal business dealings may continue if contractually or financially obliged.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses are taught that avoiding social and spiritual interaction with disfellowshipped individuals keeps the congregation free from immoral influence and that "losing precious fellowship with loved ones may help [the shunned individual] to come 'to his senses,' see the seriousness of his wrong, and take steps to return to Jehovah."<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> The practice of shunning may also serve to deter other members from dissident behavior.<sup id="cite_ref-Holden163_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden163-259">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> Members who disassociate (formally resign) are described in Watch Tower Society literature as wicked and are also shunned.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Expelled individuals may eventually be reinstated to the congregation if deemed repentant by elders in the congregation in which the disfellowshipping was enforced.<sup id="cite_ref-shepherd_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shepherd-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Reproof is a lesser form of discipline given formally by a judicial committee to a baptized Witness who is considered repentant of serious sin; the reproved person temporarily loses conspicuous privileges of service, but suffers no restriction of social or spiritual fellowship.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_congregational_discipline#Marking" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and congregational discipline">Marking</a>, a curtailing of social but not spiritual fellowship, is practiced if a baptized member persists in a course of action regarded as a violation of Bible principles but not a serious sin.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;note 4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Separateness">Separateness</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_governments" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and governments">Jehovah's Witnesses and governments</a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe that the Bible condemns the mixing of religions, on the basis that there can only be one truth from God, and therefore reject interfaith and ecumenical movements.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> They believe that only Jehovah's Witnesses represent true Christianity, and that other religions fail to meet all the requirements set by God and will soon be destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses are taught that it is vital to remain "separate from the world." The Witnesses' literature defines the "world" as "the mass of mankind apart from Jehovah's approved servants" and teach that it is morally contaminated and ruled by Satan.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses are taught that association with "worldly" people presents a "danger" to their faith,<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> and are instructed to minimize social contact with non-members to better maintain their own standards of morality.<sup id="cite_ref-holdensocial_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-holdensocial-273">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Attending <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a> is discouraged and <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">trade schools</a> are suggested as an alternative.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jehovah's Witnesses believe their highest allegiance belongs to God's kingdom, which is viewed as an actual government in heaven, with Christ as king. They remain politically neutral, do not seek public office, and are discouraged from voting, though individual members may participate in uncontroversial community improvement issues.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Although they do not take part in politics, they respect the authority of the governments under which they live.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> They do not celebrate religious holidays such as Christmas and Easter, nor do they observe birthdays, national holidays, or other celebrations they consider to honor people other than Jesus. They feel that these and many other customs have pagan origins or reflect a nationalistic or political spirit. Their position is that these traditional holidays reflect Satan's control over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> Witnesses are told that spontaneous giving at other times can help their children to not feel deprived of birthdays or other celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>They do not work in industries associated with the military, do not serve in the armed services,<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> and refuse national military service, which in some countries may result in their arrest and imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> They do not salute or pledge allegiance to flags or sing <a href="/wiki/National_anthems" class="mw-redirect" title="National anthems">national anthems</a> or patriotic songs.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses see themselves as a worldwide brotherhood that transcends national boundaries and ethnic loyalties.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Sociologist Ronald Lawson has suggested the group's intellectual and organizational isolation, coupled with the intense indoctrination of adherents, rigid internal discipline and considerable persecution, has contributed to the consistency of its sense of urgency in its apocalyptic message.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rejection_of_blood_transfusions">Rejection of blood transfusions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_blood_transfusions" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and blood transfusions">Jehovah's Witnesses and blood transfusions</a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses refuse <a href="/wiki/Blood_transfusion" title="Blood transfusion">blood transfusions</a>, which they consider a violation of God's law based on their interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Acts_15" title="Acts 15">Acts&#160;15</a>:28,&#160;29 and other scriptures.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> Since 1961 the willing acceptance of a blood transfusion by an unrepentant member has been grounds for expulsion from the group.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Members are directed to refuse blood transfusions, even in "a life-or-death situation".<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses accept non-blood alternatives and other medical procedures in lieu of blood transfusions, and their literature provides information about non-blood medical procedures.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Though Jehovah's Witnesses do not accept blood transfusions of whole blood, they may accept some <a href="/wiki/Blood_plasma_fractionation" title="Blood plasma fractionation">blood plasma fractions</a> at their own discretion.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> The Watch Tower Society provides pre-formatted <a href="/wiki/Power_of_attorney#Durable_power_of_attorney" title="Power of attorney">durable power of attorney</a> documents prohibiting major blood components, in which members can specify which allowable fractions and treatments they will personally accept.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses have established <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_and_blood_transfusions#Hospital_Liaison_Committees" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses and blood transfusions">Hospital Liaison Committees</a> as a cooperative arrangement between individual Jehovah's Witnesses and medical professionals and hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Demographics of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Demographics of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:JWStats1931-2015.png" class="image"><img alt="JWStats1931-2015.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/JWStats1931-2015.png/366px-JWStats1931-2015.png" decoding="async" width="366" height="239" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/JWStats1931-2015.png/549px-JWStats1931-2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/JWStats1931-2015.png/732px-JWStats1931-2015.png 2x" data-file-width="977" data-file-height="638" /></a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses have an active presence in most countries, but do not form a large part of the population of any country.
</p><p>For 2018, Jehovah's Witnesses reported approximately 8.58&#160;million <i>publishers</i>—the term they use for members actively involved in preaching—in about 120,000 congregations.<sup id="cite_ref-report2018_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> For the same year, they reported over 2&#160;billion hours spent in preaching activity, and conducted Bible studies with more than 10 million individuals (including those conducted by Witness parents with their children<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-report2018_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses estimate their worldwide annual growth since 2016 to be 1.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-report2018_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report2018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The official published membership statistics, such as those mentioned above, include only those who submit reports for their personal ministry;<sup id="cite_ref-jwmediastats_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jwmediastats-309">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> official statistics do not include <i>inactive</i> and <i>disfellowshipped</i> individuals or others who might attend their meetings. As a result, only about half of those who self-identified as Jehovah's Witnesses in independent demographic studies are considered <i>active</i> by the faith itself.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> The 2008 US <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Forum on Religion &amp; Public Life</a> survey found a low retention rate among members of the denomination: about 37% of people raised in the group continued to identify themselves as Jehovah's Witnesses;<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> the next lowest retention rates were for Buddhism at 50% and Catholicism at 68%. The study also found that 65% of adult Jehovah's Witnesses in the US are converts.<sup id="cite_ref-pewfact_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewfact-314">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sociological_analysis">Sociological analysis</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sociological_classifications_of_religious_movements" title="Sociological classifications of religious movements">Sociological classifications of religious movements</a></div>
<p>Sociologist <a href="/wiki/James_A._Beckford" title="James A. Beckford">James A. Beckford</a>, in his 1975 study of Jehovah's Witnesses, classified the group's organizational structure as <i>Totalizing</i>, characterized by an assertive leadership, specific and narrow objectives, control over competing demands on members' time and energy, and control over the quality of new members. Other characteristics of the classification include likelihood of friction with secular authorities, reluctance to co-operate with other religious organizations, a high rate of membership turnover, a low rate of doctrinal change, and strict uniformity of beliefs among members.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> Beckford identified the group's chief characteristics as <i>historicism</i> (identifying historical events as relating to the outworking of God's purpose), <i>absolutism</i> (conviction that Jehovah's Witness leaders dispense absolute truth), <i>activism</i> (capacity to motivate members to perform missionary tasks), <i>rationalism</i> (conviction that Witness doctrines have a rational basis devoid of mystery), <i>authoritarianism</i> (rigid presentation of regulations without the opportunity for criticism) and <i>world indifference</i> (rejection of certain secular requirements and medical treatments).<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sociologist <a href="/wiki/Bryan_R._Wilson" title="Bryan R. Wilson">Bryan R. Wilson</a>, in his consideration of five religious groups including Jehovah's Witnesses, noted that each of the denominations:<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>"exists in a state of tension with the wider society;"</li>
<li>"imposes tests of merit on would-be members;"</li>
<li>"exercises stern discipline, regulating the declared beliefs and the life habits of members and prescribing and operating sanctions for those who deviate, including the possibility of expulsion;"</li>
<li>"demands sustained and total commitment from its members, and the subordination, and perhaps even the exclusion of all other interests."</li></ol>
<p>A sociological comparative study by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> found that Jehovah's Witnesses in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> ranked highest in statistics for getting no further than high school graduation, belief in God, importance of religion in one's life, frequency of religious attendance, frequency of prayers, frequency of Bible reading outside of religious services, belief their prayers are answered, belief that their religion can only be interpreted one way, belief that theirs is the only one true faith leading to eternal life, opposition to abortion, and opposition to homosexuality. In the study, Jehovah's Witnesses ranked lowest in statistics for having an interest in politics.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> It was also among the most ethnically diverse religious groups in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-pewfact_314-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewfact-314">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Opposition">Opposition</span></h2>
<p>Controversy surrounding various beliefs, doctrines and practices of Jehovah's Witnesses has led to opposition from governments, communities, and religious groups. Religious commentator Ken Jubber wrote that "Viewed globally, this persecution has been so persistent and of such intensity that it would not be inaccurate to regard Jehovah's Witnesses as the most persecuted group of Christians of the twentieth century."<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Persecution">Persecution</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Persecution of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Persecution of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses in Nazi Germany">Persecution of Jehovah's Witnesses in Nazi Germany</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Purple_Triangle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Purple_Triangle.JPG/220px-Purple_Triangle.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Purple_Triangle.JPG/330px-Purple_Triangle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Purple_Triangle.JPG/440px-Purple_Triangle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Purple_Triangle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jehovah's Witness prisoners were identified by <a href="/wiki/Purple_triangle" title="Purple triangle">purple triangle</a> <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camp_badges" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi concentration camp badges">badges in Nazi concentration camps</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Political and religious animosity against Jehovah's Witnesses has at times led to <a href="/wiki/Mob_action" class="mw-redirect" title="Mob action">mob action</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> oppression in various countries.
Their stance regarding political neutrality and their refusal to serve in the military has led to imprisonment of members who refused conscription during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and at other times where <a href="/wiki/National_service" title="National service">national service</a> has been compulsory. Their religious activities are currently banned or restricted in some countries, including <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and some Islamic states.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>In 1933, there were approximately 20,000 Jehovah's Witnesses in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> of whom about 10,000 were imprisoned. Of those, 2,000 were sent to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">Nazi concentration camps</a>, where they were identified by <a href="/wiki/Purple_triangle" title="Purple triangle">purple triangles</a>; as many as 1,200 died, including 250 who were executed.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shulman_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shulman-325">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> during World War II, Jehovah's Witnesses were interned in camps<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup> along with political dissidents and people of Chinese and Japanese descent.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses faced discrimination in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Quiet_Revolution" title="Quiet Revolution">Quiet Revolution</a>, including bans on distributing literature or holding meetings.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 1951, about 9,300 Jehovah's Witnesses in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> were deported to <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_North" title="Operation North">Operation North</a> in April 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-passat_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-passat-332">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In April 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Russia" title="Supreme Court of Russia">Supreme Court of Russia</a> labeled Jehovah's Witnesses an extremist organization, banned its activities in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and issued an order to confiscate the organization's assets.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Authors including <a href="/wiki/William_J._Whalen" title="William J. Whalen">William Whalen</a>, Shawn Francis Peters and former Witnesses <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Grizzuti_Harrison" title="Barbara Grizzuti Harrison">Barbara Grizzuti Harrison</a>, Alan Rogerson and William Schnell have claimed the arrests and mob violence in the United States in the 1930s and 1940s were the consequence of what appeared to be a deliberate course of provocation of authorities and other religious groups by Jehovah's Witnesses. Whalen, Harrison and Schnell have suggested Rutherford invited and cultivated opposition for publicity purposes in a bid to attract dispossessed members of society, and to convince members that persecution from the outside world was evidence of the truth of their struggle to serve God.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> Watch Tower Society literature of the period directed that Witnesses should "never seek a controversy" nor resist arrest, but also advised members not to co-operate with police officers or courts that ordered them to stop preaching, and to prefer jail rather than pay fines.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_challenges">Legal challenges</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_cases_involving_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_by_country" title="Supreme Court cases involving Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses by country">Supreme Court cases involving Jehovah's Witnesses by country</a></div>
<p>Several cases involving Jehovah's Witnesses have been heard by Supreme Courts throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> The cases generally relate to their right to practice their religion, displays of patriotism and military service, and blood transfusions.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the United States, legal challenges by Jehovah's Witnesses prompted a series of state and federal court rulings that reinforced judicial protections for civil liberties.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> Among the rights strengthened by Witness court victories in the United States are the protection of religious conduct from federal and state interference, the right to abstain from patriotic rituals and military service, the right of patients to refuse medical treatment, and the right to engage in public discourse.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> Similar cases in their favor have been heard in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversy">Criticism and controversy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Criticism of Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Criticism of Jehovah's Witnesses</a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses have received criticism from mainstream Christianity, members of the medical community, former members and commentators regarding <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_beliefs" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses beliefs">their beliefs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses_practices" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses practices">practices</a>. The movement has been accused of doctrinal inconsistency and reversals, failed predictions, mistranslation of the Bible, harsh treatment of former members and autocratic and coercive leadership. Criticism has also focused on their rejection of <a href="/wiki/Blood_transfusions" class="mw-redirect" title="Blood transfusions">blood transfusions</a>, particularly in life-threatening medical situations, and failing to report cases of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> to the authorities. Many of the claims are denied by Jehovah's Witnesses and some have also been disputed by courts and religious scholars.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_speech_and_thought">Free speech and thought</span></h3>
<p>Doctrines of Jehovah's Witnesses are established by the Governing Body.<sup id="cite_ref-Holden22_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden22-345">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-346">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> The denomination does not tolerate dissent over doctrines and practices;<sup id="cite_ref-voice_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-voice-159">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Beckford_dissent_349-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beckford_dissent-349">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup> members who openly disagree with the group's teachings are expelled and shunned.<sup id="cite_ref-Muramoto_254-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muramoto-254">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> Witness publications strongly discourage followers from questioning doctrine and counsel received from the Governing Body, reasoning that it is to be trusted as part of "God's organization".<sup id="cite_ref-Beckford_dissent_349-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beckford_dissent-349">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> It also warns members to "avoid independent thinking", claiming such thinking "was introduced by Satan the Devil"<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> and would "cause division".<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup> Those who openly disagree with official teachings are condemned as "apostates" who are "mentally diseased".<sup id="cite_ref-Holden163_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden163-259">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Former members Heather and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Botting" title="Gary Botting">Gary Botting</a> compare the cultural paradigms of the denomination to <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Nineteen_Eighty-four" class="mw-redirect" title="Nineteen Eighty-four">Nineteen Eighty-four</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup> and Alan Rogerson describes the group's leadership as <a href="/wiki/Totalitarianism" title="Totalitarianism">totalitarian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> Other critics charge that by disparaging individual decision-making, the group's leaders cultivate a system of unquestioning obedience<sup id="cite_ref-Bevindependent_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevindependent-165">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> in which Witnesses abrogate all responsibility and rights over their personal lives.<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> Critics also accuse the group's leaders of exercising "intellectual dominance" over Witnesses,<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> controlling information<sup id="cite_ref-Muramoto_254-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muramoto-254">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> and creating "mental isolation", which former Governing Body member <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Franz" title="Raymond Franz">Raymond Franz</a> argued were all elements of <a href="/wiki/Mind_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Mind control">mind control</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jehovah's Witness publications state that consensus of faith aids unity, and deny that unity restricts individuality or imagination.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> Historian James Irvin Lichti has rejected the description of the denomination as "totalitarian".<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Sociologist <a href="/wiki/Rodney_Stark" title="Rodney Stark">Rodney Stark</a> states that Jehovah's Witness leaders are "not always very democratic" and that members "are expected to conform to rather strict standards," but adds that "enforcement tends to be very informal, sustained by the close bonds of friendship within the group", and that Jehovah's Witnesses see themselves as "part of the power structure rather than subject to it."<sup id="cite_ref-Stark_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stark-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Sociologist Andrew Holden states that most members who join millenarian movements such as Jehovah's Witnesses have made an informed choice.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> However, he also states that defectors "are seldom allowed a dignified exit",<sup id="cite_ref-Holden163_259-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden163-259">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> and describes the administration as <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocratic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Holden22_345-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holden22-345">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_World_Translation">New World Translation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_World_Translation_of_the_Holy_Scriptures" title="New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures">New World Translation of the Holy Scriptures</a></div>
<p>Various Bible scholars, including <a href="/wiki/Bruce_M._Metzger" title="Bruce M. Metzger">Bruce M. Metzger</a><sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MacLean_Gilmour" title="MacLean Gilmour">MacLean Gilmour</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> have said that while scholarship is evident in <i>New World Translation</i>, its rendering of certain texts are inaccurate and biased in favor of Witness practices and doctrines.<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-haas_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haas-374">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ankerberg_375-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ankerberg-375">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pentonbible_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pentonbible-376">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> Critics of the group such as Edmund C. Gruss,<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> and Christian writers such as <a href="/wiki/Ray_Stedman" title="Ray Stedman">Ray C. Stedman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walter_Ralston_Martin" title="Walter Ralston Martin">Walter Martin</a>, Norman Klann<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_A._Hoekema" title="Anthony A. Hoekema">Anthony Hoekema</a><sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> state that the <i>New World Translation</i> exhibits scholastic dishonesty. Most criticism of the <i>New World Translation</i> relates to its rendering of the New Testament, particularly regarding the introduction of the name <i>Jehovah</i> and in passages related to the Trinity doctrine.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unfulfilled_predictions">Unfulfilled predictions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Watch_Tower_Society_unfulfilled_predictions" title="Watch Tower Society unfulfilled predictions">Watch Tower Society unfulfilled predictions</a></div>
<p>Watch Tower Society publications have claimed that God has used Jehovah's Witnesses (and formerly, the International Bible Students) to declare his will<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup> and has provided advance knowledge about <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">Armageddon</a> and the establishment of <a href="/wiki/God%27s_kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="God&#39;s kingdom">God's kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup> Some publications also claimed that God has used Jehovah's Witnesses and the International Bible Students as a modern-day prophet.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;note 5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_D._Chryssides" class="mw-redirect" title="George D. Chryssides">George D. Chryssides</a> stated, "while prediction may be part of a biblical prophet's role, the root meaning of prophecy is that of proclaiming God's word." He went on to say that, "Jehovah's Witnesses ... are the recipients of prophecy, who regard themselves as invested with the interpretation of biblical writings."<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;note 6&#93;</a></sup> With these interpretations, Jehovah's Witnesses' publications have made various predictions about world events they believe were prophesied in the Bible.<sup id="cite_ref-WT59_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WT59-391">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> Failed predictions have led to the alteration or abandonment of some doctrines.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup> Some failed predictions had been presented as "beyond doubt" or "approved by God".<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Watch Tower Society rejects accusations that it is a <a href="/wiki/False_prophet" title="False prophet">false prophet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_396-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-396">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup> stating that its interpretations are not inspired or infallible,<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup> and that it has not claimed its predictions were "the words of Jehovah."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_396-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-396">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup> Chryssides has suggested that with the exception of statements about 1914, 1925 and 1975, the changing views and dates of the Jehovah's Witnesses are largely attributable to changed understandings of biblical chronology rather than to failed predictions.<sup id="cite_ref-Georgie_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Georgie-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Chryssides further states, "it is therefore simplistic and naïve to view the Witnesses as a group that continues to set a single end-date that fails and then devise a new one, as many counter-cultists do."<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup> However, sociologist Andrew Holden states that since the foundation of the movement around 140 years ago, "Witnesses have maintained that we are living on the precipice of the end of time."<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Handling_of_sexual_abuse_cases">Handling of sexual abuse cases</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses%27_handling_of_child_sex_abuse" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses&#39; handling of child sex abuse">Jehovah's Witnesses' handling of child sex abuse</a></div>
<p>Jehovah's Witnesses have been accused of having policies and culture that help to conceal cases of sexual abuse within the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-ousted_402-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ousted-402">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> The group has been criticized for its "two witness rule" for church discipline, based on its application of scriptures at Deuteronomy 19:15 and Matthew 18:15–17, which requires sexual abuse to be substantiated by secondary evidence if the accused person denies any wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-sexmedia_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexmedia-403">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup> In cases where corroboration is lacking, the Watch Tower Society's instruction is that "the elders will leave the matter in Jehovah's hands".<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup> A former member of the headquarters staff, Barbara Anderson, says the policy effectively requires that there be another witness to an act of molestation, "which is an impossibility". Anderson says the policies "protect pedophiles rather than protect the children."<sup id="cite_ref-NBC_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC-407">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> Jehovah's Witnesses maintain that they have a strong policy to protect children, adding that the best way to protect children is by educating parents; they also state that they do not sponsor activities that separate children from parents.<sup id="cite_ref-cpt_E_408-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cpt_E-408">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sexmedia_403-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexmedia-403">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The group's failure to report abuse allegations to authorities has also been criticized.<sup id="cite_ref-MediaWales_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediaWales-411">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup> The Watch Tower Society's policy is that elders inform authorities when required by law to do so, but otherwise leave that action up to the victim and his or her family.<sup id="cite_ref-sexmedia_403-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexmedia-403">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">&#91;407&#93;</a></sup> The Australian <a href="/wiki/Royal_Commission_into_Institutional_Responses_to_Child_Sexual_Abuse" title="Royal Commission into Institutional Responses to Child Sexual Abuse">Royal Commission into Institutional Responses to Child Sexual Abuse</a> found that of 1,006 alleged perpetrators of child sexual abuse investigated by Jehovah's Witness elders since 1950, "not one was reported by the church to secular authorities."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_346-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-346">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup> The Royal Commission also found that the Watch Tower Society legal department routinely provided incorrect information to elders based on an incorrect understanding about what constitutes a legal obligation to report crimes in Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">&#91;408&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">&#91;409&#93;</a></sup> William Bowen, a former Jehovah's Witness elder who established the <a href="/wiki/Silentlambs" title="Silentlambs">Silentlambs</a> organization to assist sex abuse victims within the denomination, has claimed Witness leaders discourage followers from reporting incidents of sexual misconduct to authorities, and other critics claim the organization is reluctant to alert authorities in order to protect its "crime-free" reputation.<sup id="cite_ref-ousted_402-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ousted-402">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">&#91;410&#93;</a></sup> In court cases in the United Kingdom and the United States the Watch Tower Society has been found to have been negligent in its failure to protect children from known sex offenders within the congregation,<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">&#91;411&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">&#91;412&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">&#91;413&#93;</a></sup> and the Society has settled other child abuse lawsuits out of court, reportedly paying as much as $780,000 to one plaintiff without admitting wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-NBC_407-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBC-407">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Charity_Commission_for_England_and_Wales" title="Charity Commission for England and Wales">Charity Commission for England and Wales</a> began an inquiry into Jehovah's Witnesses' handling of allegations of child sexual abuse in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCBuchanan_420-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCBuchanan-420">&#91;414&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-421">&#91;415&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>

June 15, 2006. p.&#160;26. <q>We too should remain faithful to Jehovah and to his organization regardless of injustices we suffer and regardless of what others do.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Your+Reminders+Are+What+I+Am+Fond+Of&amp;rft.pages=26&amp;rft.date=2006-06-15&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F2006446&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><br /> <cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/2006366">"Are You Prepared for Survival?"</a>. <i>The Watchtower</i>. May 15, 2006. p.&#160;22. <q>Just as Noah and his God-fearing family were preserved in the ark, survival of individuals today depends on their faith and their loyal association with the earthly part of Jehovah's universal organization.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Are+You+Prepared+for+Survival%3F&amp;rft.pages=22&amp;rft.date=2006-05-15&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F2006366&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><br /> <cite class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1102002074"><i>Worship The Only True God</i></a>. </li>
<li id="cite_note-143"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-143">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/302013019"><i>2013 Yearbook of Jehovah's Witnesses</i></a>. p.&#160;178. <q>During the 2012 service year, Jehovah's Witnesses spent over $184 million in caring for special pioneers, missionaries, and traveling overseers in their field service assignments.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=2013+Yearbook+of+Jehovah%27s+Witnesses&amp;rft.pages=178&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F302013019&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-264"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-264">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A common example given is a baptized Witness who dates a non-Witness; see <cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1999527">"Questions From Readers"</a>. <i>The Watchtower</i>. July 15, 1999. p.&#160;30.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Questions+From+Readers&amp;rft.pages=30&amp;rft.date=1999-07-15&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1999527&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-388"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-388">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Raymond Franz cites numerous examples. In <i>Crisis of Conscience</i>, 2002, pg. 173, he quotes from <cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1972241">"They Shall Know That a Prophet Was Among Them"</a>. <i>The Watchtower</i>. April 1, 1972. pp.&#160;197–200.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=They+Shall+Know+That+a+Prophet+Was+Among+Them&amp;rft.pages=197-200&amp;rft.date=1972-04-01&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1972241&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> which states that God had raised Jehovah's Witnesses as a prophet "to warn (people) of dangers and declare things to come". He also cites <cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1997323">"Identifying the Right Kind of Messenger"</a>. <i>The Watchtower</i>. May 1, 1997. p.&#160;8.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Identifying+the+Right+Kind+of+Messenger&amp;rft.pages=8&amp;rft.date=1997-05-01&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1997323&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> which identifies the Witnesses as his "true messengers ... by making the messages he delivers through them come true", in contrast to "false messengers", whose predictions fail. In <i>In Search of Christian Freedom,</i> 2007, he quotes <cite class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1101971004"><i>Commissioned to Speak in the Divine Name</i></a>. Watchtower Bible and Tract Society. 1971. pp.&#160;70, 292.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Commissioned+to+Speak+in+the+Divine+Name&amp;rft.pages=70%2C+292&amp;rft.pub=Watchtower+Bible+and+Tract+Society&amp;rft.date=1971&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1101971004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> which describes Witnesses as the modern Ezekiel class, "a genuine prophet within our generation". The Watch Tower book noted: "Concerning the message faithfully delivered by the Ezekiel class, Jehovah positively states that it 'must come true' ... those who wait undecided until it does 'come true' will also have to know that a prophet himself had proved to be in the midst of them." He also cites <cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1980765">"Execution of the Great Harlot Nears"</a>. <i>The Watchtower</i>. October 15, 1980. p.&#160;17.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Execution+of+the+Great+Harlot+Nears&amp;rft.pages=17&amp;rft.date=1980-10-15&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1980765&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> which claims God gives the Witnesses "special knowledge that others do not have ... advance knowledge about this system's end".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-390"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-390">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <i>Jehovah's Witnesses Continuity and Change</i> Chryssides states, after discussing the April 1, 1972 <i>Watchtower</i> article, that, "It would be tedious to comment on each passage in which Watch Tower literature explains the Jehovah's Witnesses' position on prophecy. Some of it may lack the precision that its detractors appear to demand, but the Society's position is quite clear. Jehovah's Witnesses do not claim to have any new revelation or people who are designated as prophets. As cessationists, they identify the ability to prophesy as a gift that died out with the first generation of Christians, but prophetic utterances remain in the Bible, which serves as the key source of authority. ... since the Bible is held to contain predictive prophecy, Jehovah's Witnesses claim to see into the future through the Society's interpretation of scripture." pg 225.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Michael Hill, ed. (1972). <li id="cite_note-name1-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-name1_11-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-name1_11-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Rogerson, Alan (1969). <i>Millions Now Living Will Never Die: A Study of Jehovah's Witnesses</i>. London: Constable. p.&#160;55. <q>In 1931, came an important milestone in the history of the organization. For many years Rutherford's followers had been called a variety of names: 'International Bible Students', 'Russellites', or 'Millennial Dawners'. In order to distinguish clearly his followers from the other groups who had separated in 1918 Rutherford proposed that they adopt an entirely new name—<i>Jehovah's witnesses</i>.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Millions+Now+Living+Will+Never+Die%3A+A+Study+of+Jehovah%27s+Witnesses&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pages=55&amp;rft.pub=Constable&amp;rft.date=1969&amp;rft.au=Rogerson%2C+Alan&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-name3-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-name3_13-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-name3_13-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation magazine">"A New Name". <i>The Watch Tower</i>. Russell there have arisen numerous companies formed out of those who once walked with him, each of these companies claiming to teach the truth, and each calling themselves by some name, such as "Followers of Pastor Russell", "those who stand by the truth as expounded by Pastor Russell," "Associated Bible Students," and some by the names of their local leaders. All of this tends to confusion and hinders those of good will who are not better informed from obtaining a knowledge of the truth.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watch+Tower&amp;rft.atitle=A+New+Name&amp;rft.pages=291&amp;rft.date=1931-10-01&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

Russell was concerned that his supporters should feel part of a unified movement."</span>

<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-59">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Crompton, Robert (1996). <i>Counting the Days to Armageddon</i>. Cambridge: James Clarke &amp; Co. pp.&#160;84–85. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-227-67939-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-227-67939-5"><bdi>978-0-227-67939-5</bdi></a>. <q>One of Rutherford's first actions as president ... was, without reference either to his fellow directors or to the editorial committee which Russell had nominated in his will, to commission a seventh volume of <i>Studies in the Scriptures</i>. Responsibility for preparing this volume was given to two of Russell's close associates, George H. Fisher and Clayton J. Woodworth. On the face of it, their brief was to edit for publication the notes left by Russell ... and to draw upon his published writings ... It is obvious ... that it was not in any straightforward sense the result of editing Russell's papers, rather it was in large measure the original work of Woodworth and Fisher at the behest of the new president.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Counting+the+Days+to+Armageddon&amp;rft.place=Cambridge&amp;rft.pages=84-85&amp;rft.pub=James+Clarke+%26+Co&amp;rft.date=1996&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-227-67939-5&amp;rft.aulast=Crompton&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-73">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Reed, David, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110909064529/http://journal.equip.org/articles/whither-the-watchtower-">Whither the Watchtower?</a> <i>Christian Research Journal</i>, Summer 1993, pg 27: "By gradually replacing locally elected elders with his own appointees, he managed to transform a loose collection of semi-autonomous, democratically run congregations into a tight-knit organizational machine controlled from his office. Some local congregations broke away, forming such groups as the Chicago Bible Students, the Dawn Bible Students, and the Laymen's Home Missionary Movement, all of which continue to this day."</span>

<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Thirty Years a Watchtower Slave</i>, William J. <li id="cite_note-99"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-99">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1980207">"The Watchtower"</a>. March 15, 1980. pp.&#160;17–18. <q>With the appearance of the book <i>Life Everlasting—in Freedom of the Sons of God</i>, ... considerable expectation was aroused regarding the year 1975. ... there were other statements published that implied that such realization of hopes by that year was more of a probability than a mere possibility. It is to be regretted that these latter statements apparently overshadowed the cautionary ones and contributed to a buildup of the expectation already initiated. ... <i>persons having to do with the publication of the information</i> ... contributed to the buildup of hopes centered on that date.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.pages=17-18&amp;rft.date=1980-03-15&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1980207&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span> <span class="cs1-hidden-error error citation-comment">Cite magazine requires <code class="cs1-code">&#124;magazine=</code> (<a href="/wiki/Help:CS1_errors#missing_periodical" title="Help:CS1 errors">help</a>)</span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

We should have confidence in the channel God is using.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Do+We+Need+Help+to+Understand+the+Bible%3F&amp;rft.pages=19&amp;rft.date=1981-02-15&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1981127&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

February 1, 1952. p.&#160;69.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Is+Interfaith+God%27s+Way%3F&amp;rft.pages=69&amp;rft.date=1952-02-01&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1952081&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-267"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-267">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFBeckford1975">Beckford 1975</a>, p.&#160;202, "The ideological argument states that, since absolute truth is unitary and exclusive of all relativisation, there can only 'logically' be one human organization to represent it. Consequently, all other religious organizations are in error and are to be strictly avoided. The absolutist view of truth further implies that, since anything less than absolute truth can only corrupt and destroy it, there can be no justification for Jehovah's witnesses having any kind of association with other religionists, however sincere the motivation might be."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-290"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-290">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ronald Lawson, "Sect-state relations: Accounting for the differing trajectories of Seventh-Day Adventists and Jehovah's Witnesses", <i>Sociology of Religion</i>, Winter 1995, "The urgency of the Witness's apocalyptic has changed very little over time. The intellectual isolation of the Witness leaders has allowed them to retain their traditional position, and it is they who continue to be the chief purveyors of the radical eschataology ....This commitment (to principle) was bolstered by their organizational isolation, intense indoctrination of adherents, rigid internal discipline, and considerable persecution."</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-355"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-355">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation magazine"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://wol.jw.org/en/wol/d/r1/lp-e/1964324">"Building a Firm Foundation in Christ"</a>. <i>The Watchtower</i>. May 1, 1964. pp.&#160;277–278. <q>It is through the columns of The Watchtower that Jehovah provides direction and constant Scriptural counsel to his people, and it requires careful study and attention to details in order to apply this information, to get a full understanding of the principles involved, and to assure ourselves of right thinking on these matters. It is in this way that we "are thoroughly able to grasp mentally with all the holy ones" the fullness of our commission and of the preaching responsibility that Jehovah has placed on all Christians as footstep followers of his Son. Any other course would produce independent thinking and cause division.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Watchtower&amp;rft.atitle=Building+a+Firm+Foundation+in+Christ&amp;rft.pages=277-278&amp;rft.date=1964-05-01&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwol.jw.org%2Fen%2Fwol%2Fd%2Fr1%2Flp-e%2F1964324&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-sexmedia-403"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-sexmedia_403-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sexmedia_403-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-sexmedia_403-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20091123144858/http://www.jw-media.org/aboutjw/article23.htm">"Jehovah's Witnesses and Child Protection"</a>. Jehovah's Witnesses Official Media website. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jw-media.org/aboutjw/article23.htm">the original</a> on November 23, 2009.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Jehovah%27s+Witnesses+and+Child+Protection&amp;rft.pub=Jehovah%27s+Witnesses+Official+Media+website&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.jw-media.org%2Faboutjw%2Farticle23.htm&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-404"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-404">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation report"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.childabuseroyalcommission.gov.au/sites/default/files/file-list/Case%20Study%2029%20-%20Transcript%20-%20Jehovahs%20Witnesses%20-%20Day%20152%20-%2004082015.pdf">Public Hearing - Case Study 29 (Day 152)</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. <i>Royal Commission into Institutional Responses to Child Sexual Abuse, Australia</i> (Report). p.&#160;67,72. <q>in the absence of a confession or circumstantial evidence or other indicators, would we act judicially on one witness as the courts would do, the answer would be no, and I don't see that changing, in harmony with the scriptures. ... Q. Insofar as a second witness is concerned, is that requirement covered by, for example, scientific evidence? A. Certainly. Q. So if there was some external forensic scientific or direct evidence which is not of an observer to the incident, but someone who observes some corroborative aspect to the incident, that would be sufficient, would it? A. The answer is yes... we, as the case files will show, have disfellowshipped people for being in an inappropriate setting where there is some allegation.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=report&amp;rft.btitle=Public+Hearing+-+Case+Study+29+%28Day+152%29&amp;rft.pages=67%2C72&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.childabuseroyalcommission.gov.au%2Fsites%2Fdefault%2Ffiles%2Ffile-list%2FCase%2520Study%252029%2520-%2520Transcript%2520-%2520Jehovahs%2520Witnesses%2520-%2520Day%2520152%2520-%252004082015.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AJehovah%27s+Witnesses" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
